The **Philippines**,[^6] officially the **Republic of the Philippines**,[^7] is an [archipelagic country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archipelagic_state "Archipelagic state") in [Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"). Located in the western [Pacific Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean"), it consists of about [7,641 islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Philippines "List of islands of the Philippines"), with a total area of about 300,000 square kilometers, which are broadly categorized in [three main geographical divisions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Island_groups_of_the_Philippines "Island groups of the Philippines") from north to south: [Luzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luzon "Luzon"), [Visayas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visayas "Visayas"), and [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao"). With a population of over 114 million, it is the world's [twelfth-most-populous country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population").

The Philippines is bounded by the [South China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea "South China Sea") to the west, the [Philippine Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Sea "Philippine Sea") to the east, and the [Celebes Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celebes_Sea "Celebes Sea") to the south. It shares [maritime borders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maritime_border "Maritime border") with [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") to the north, [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan "Japan") to the northeast, [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau") to the east and southeast, [Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia") to the south, [Malaysia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia") to the southwest, [Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam") to the west, and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") to the northwest. It has [diverse ethnicities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_the_Philippines "Ethnic groups in the Philippines") and [a rich culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_the_Philippines "Culture of the Philippines"). [Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila "Manila") is [the country's capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_of_the_Philippines "Capital of the Philippines"), and [its most populated city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cities_of_the_Philippines#Largest_cities "Cities of the Philippines") is [Quezon City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quezon_City "Quezon City"). Both are within [Metro Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metro_Manila "Metro Manila").

[Negritos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negrito "Negrito"), the archipelago's earliest inhabitants, were followed by [waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Models_of_migration_to_the_Philippines "Models of migration to the Philippines") of [Austronesian peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austronesian_peoples "Austronesian peoples"). The adoption of [animism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animism "Animism"), [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism") with [Buddhist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist "Buddhist") influence, and [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam") established [island-kingdoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_\(900%E2%80%931565\) "History of the Philippines (900–1565)"). Extensive overseas trade with neighbors such as the late [Tang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tang_dynasty "Tang dynasty") or [Song](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Song "Southern Song") empire brought [Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sangley "Sangley") people to the archipelago as well, who would also gradually settle in and [intermix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interethnic_marriage "Interethnic marriage") over the centuries. The arrival of the explorer [Ferdinand Magellan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan "Ferdinand Magellan") marked the beginning of [Spanish colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Colonization_in_the_Philippines "Spanish Colonization in the Philippines"). In 1543, Spanish explorer [Ruy López de Villalobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos "Ruy López de Villalobos") named the archipelago *las Islas Filipinas* in honor of [King Philip II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain "Philip II of Spain"). [Catholicism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") became the dominant religion, and Manila became the western hub of [trans-Pacific trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet "Spanish treasure fleet"). [Hispanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spaniard "Spaniard") immigrants from [Latin America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_American_Asian "Latin American Asian") and [Iberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iberia "Iberia") would also selectively colonize. The [Philippine Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Revolution "Philippine Revolution") began in 1896, and became entwined with the 1898 [Spanish–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War "Spanish–American War"). Spain ceded the territory to the United States, and [Filipino revolutionaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_Junta "Hong Kong Junta") declared the [First Philippine Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic "First Philippine Republic"). The ensuing [Philippine–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War "Philippine–American War") ended with the United States controlling the territory until the [Japanese invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines_campaign_\(1941%E2%80%931942\) "Philippines campaign (1941–1942)") of the islands during [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"). After [the United States retook the Philippines from the Japanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines_campaign_\(1944%E2%80%931945\) "Philippines campaign (1944–1945)"), the Philippines became independent in 1946. Since then, the country notably experienced a [period of martial law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law_under_Ferdinand_Marcos "Martial law under Ferdinand Marcos") from 1972 to 1981 under the dictatorship of [Ferdinand Marcos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_Marcos "Ferdinand Marcos") and his subsequent overthrow by the [People Power Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People_Power_Revolution "People Power Revolution") in 1986, returning to democracy.

The Philippines is an [emerging market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emerging_market "Emerging market") and a [developing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developing_country "Developing country") and [newly industrialized country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newly_industrialized_country "Newly industrialized country"), [whose economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_Philippines "Economy of the Philippines") is transitioning from being agricultural to service- and manufacturing-centered. It has a variety of natural resources and a globally-significant [level of biodiversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_countries "Megadiverse countries"). The country is also part of [multiple international organizations and forums](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_organization_membership_of_the_Philippines "International organization membership of the Philippines"), mainly in [ASEAN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ASEAN "ASEAN"). Despite its fast economic growth, it continues to struggle with [inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Income_inequality_in_the_Philippines "Income inequality in the Philippines"), widespread [corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption_in_the_Philippines "Corruption in the Philippines"), and vulnerability to natural disasters due to its location within the Pacific [Ring of Fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ring_of_Fire "Ring of Fire"), and to the equator, making it prone to [earthquakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_the_Philippines "List of earthquakes in the Philippines"), [monsoon rains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsoon "Monsoon"), and [typhoons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoons_in_the_Philippines "Typhoons in the Philippines"), to which the Philippines has built a [resilience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_resilience "Community resilience").

## Etymology

During his 1542 expedition, Spanish explorer [Ruy López de Villalobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos "Ruy López de Villalobos") named the islands of [Leyte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leyte "Leyte") and [Samar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samar "Samar") " *Felipinas* " after the [Prince of Asturias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias "Prince of Asturias"), later [Philip II of Castile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_II_of_Castile "Philip II of Castile"). Eventually, the name " *Las Islas Filipinas* " would be used for the archipelago's Spanish possessions.[^25]<sup><span title="Page: 6">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=15KZU-yMuisC&amp;pg=PA6">6</a> </span></sup> Other names, such as " *Islas del Poniente* " (Western Islands), " *Islas del Oriente* " (Eastern Islands), Ferdinand Magellan's name, and " *San Lázaro* " (Islands of St. Lazarus), were used by the Spanish to refer to islands in the region before Spanish rule was established.[^26] [^27] [^28]

During the [Philippine Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Revolution "Philippine Revolution"), the [Malolos Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malolos_Congress "Malolos Congress") proclaimed it the *República Filipina* ([Philippine Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic "First Philippine Republic")).[^29] American colonial authorities referred to the country as the Philippine Islands (a translation of the Spanish name).[^30] The [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") began changing its nomenclature from "the Philippine Islands" to "the Philippines" in the Philippine Autonomy Act and the [Jones Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jones_Law_\(Philippines\) "Jones Law (Philippines)").[^31] The official title "Republic of the Philippines" was included in the 1935 constitution as the name of the future independent state,[^32] and in all succeeding constitutional revisions.[^33] [^34]

## History

### Prehistory (pre–900)

![A burial jar with its lid decorated with two people on a boat](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Manunggul_Jar.jpg/250px-Manunggul_Jar.jpg)

The Manunggul burial jar, one of the numerous burial jars found on the cave system

There is [evidence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaeology_of_the_Philippines "Archaeology of the Philippines") of early [hominins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominins "Hominins") living in what is now the Philippines as early as 709,000 years ago.[^35] Bones from [Callao Cave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Callao_Cave "Callao Cave") potentially represent an otherwise unknown species, *[Homo luzonensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_luzonensis "Homo luzonensis")*, who lived 50,000 to 67,000 years ago.[^36] [^37] The oldest [modern human](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_human "Modern human") remains on the islands are from the [Tabon Caves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabon_Caves "Tabon Caves") of [Palawan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palawan "Palawan"), [U/Th-dated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U/Th-dated "U/Th-dated") to 47,000 ± 11–10,000 years ago.[^38] [Tabon Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabon_Man "Tabon Man") is presumably a [Negrito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negrito "Negrito"), among the archipelago's earliest inhabitants descended from the first human migrations out of Africa via the coastal route along [southern Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia "South Asia") to the now-sunken landmasses of [Sundaland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sundaland "Sundaland") and [Sahul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sahul "Sahul").[^39]

The first Austronesians reached the Philippines from Taiwan around 2200 BC, settling the [Batanes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batanes "Batanes") Islands (where they built stone fortresses known as *[ijangs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ijang "Ijang")*) [^40] and northern [Luzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luzon "Luzon"). Jade artifacts have been dated to 2000 BC,[^41] [^42] with [lingling-o](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lingling-o "Lingling-o") jade items made in Luzon with raw materials from Taiwan.[^43] By 1000 BC, the inhabitants of the archipelago had developed into four societies: [hunter-gatherer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter-gatherer "Hunter-gatherer") tribes, warrior societies, highland [plutocracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutocracies "Plutocracies"), and port principalities.[^44] The Philippines prior to foreign colonization was believed to be egalitarian.[^45]

### Early states (900–1565)

The earliest known surviving written record in the Philippines is the 900 AD [Laguna Copperplate Inscription](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription "Laguna Copperplate Inscription"), which was written in [Old Malay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Malay "Old Malay") using the early [Kawi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kawi_alphabet "Kawi alphabet") script.[^46] By the 14th century, several large coastal settlements emerged as trading centers and became the focus of [societal changes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_achievements_of_pre-colonial_Philippines "Cultural achievements of pre-colonial Philippines").[^47] Some [polities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polities "Polities") had exchanges with other states throughout Asia.[^48]<sup><span title="Page: 3">: 3</span> </sup> [^49] Trade with China began during the late [Tang dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tang_dynasty "Tang dynasty"),[^50] [^51] and expanded during the [Song dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Song_dynasty "Song dynasty").[^52] [^53] [^51] Throughout the second millennium AD, some polities were part of the [tributary system of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tributary_system_of_China "Tributary system of China").[^25]<sup><span title="Pages: 177–178">: 177–178</span> </sup> [^48]<sup><span title="Page: 3">: 3</span> </sup> With extensive trade and diplomacy, this brought [Southern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_and_southern_China "Northern and southern China") [Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Han_Chinese "Han Chinese") merchants and migrants from [Southern Fujian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Fujian "Southern Fujian"),[^54] [^55] [^56] who would gradually settle and intermix in the Philippines. Indian cultural traits such as linguistic terms and religious practices [began to spread](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_influences_in_early_Philippine_polities "Indian influences in early Philippine polities") in the Philippines during the 14th century, via the Indianized Hindu [Majapahit Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majapahit "Majapahit").[^57] [^58] By the 15th century, Islam was established in the [Sulu Archipelago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulu_Archipelago "Sulu Archipelago") and spread from there.[^47]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Naturales_4.png/250px-Naturales_4.png)

A couple portrayed in 1590's Early Spanish colonial period of the Philippines, draped in gold

Polities founded in the Philippines between the 10th and 16th centuries include [Maynila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maynila_\(historical_polity\) "Maynila (historical polity)"),[^59] [Tondo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tondo_\(historical_polity\) "Tondo (historical polity)"), [Namayan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namayan "Namayan"), [Pangasinan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pangasinan_\(historical_polity\) "Pangasinan (historical polity)"), [Caboloan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caboloan "Caboloan"), [Cebu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cebu_\(historical_state\) "Cebu (historical state)"), [Butuan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butuan_\(historical_polity\) "Butuan (historical polity)"), [Maguindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Maguindanao "Sultanate of Maguindanao"), [Lanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_Lanao "Confederate States of Lanao"), [Sulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Sulu "Sultanate of Sulu"), and [Ma-i](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma-i "Ma-i").[^60] The early polities typically had a three-tier social structure: nobility, freemen, and dependent debtor-bondsmen.[^48]<sup><span title="Page: 3">: 3</span> </sup> [^61]<sup><span title="Page: 672">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=6Pn0Pfh1Cl0C&amp;pg=PA672">672</a> </span></sup> Among the nobility were leaders known as [datus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Datu "Datu"), who were responsible for ruling autonomous groups ([barangays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precolonial_barangay "Precolonial barangay") or dulohan).[^62] When the barangays banded together to form a larger settlement or a geographically looser alliance,[^48]<sup><span title="Page: 3">: 3</span> </sup> [^63] their more-esteemed members would be recognized as a " [paramount datu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramount_rulers_in_early_Philippine_history "Paramount rulers in early Philippine history") ",[^64]<sup><span title="Page: 58">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=A40BEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA58">58</a> </span></sup> [^44] [rajah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajah "Rajah") or [sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultan "Sultan"),[^65] and would rule the community.[^66] Population density is thought to have been low during the 14th to 16th centuries [^64]<sup><span title="Page: 18">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=A40BEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA18">18</a> </span></sup> due to the [frequency of typhoons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon#Frequency "Typhoon") and the Philippines' location on the Pacific [Ring of Fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ring_of_Fire "Ring of Fire").[^67] Portuguese explorer [Ferdinand Magellan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan "Ferdinand Magellan") arrived in 1521, claimed the islands for Spain, and was killed by [Lapulapu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lapulapu "Lapulapu") 's men in the [Battle of Mactan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mactan "Battle of Mactan").[^68]<sup><span title="Page: 21">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=2Z-n_kDTxf0C&amp;pg=PT46">21</a> </span></sup> [^69]<sup><span title="Page: 261">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=wmgX9M_yETIC&amp;pg=PA261">261</a></span></sup>

### Spanish and American colonial rule (1565–1934)

![See caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Vista_del_Puente_de_Manila_%281847%29.png/250px-Vista_del_Puente_de_Manila_%281847%29.png)

Manila, 1847

Unification and colonization by the [Crown of Castile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_of_Castile "Crown of Castile") began when Spanish explorer [Miguel López de Legazpi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi "Miguel López de Legazpi") arrived from [New Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Spain "New Spain") in 1565.[^70] [^71] [^72]<sup><span title="Pages: 20–23">: 20–23</span> </sup> Many [Filipinos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filipinos "Filipinos") were brought to New Spain [as slaves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Spanish_slavery_in_the_Philippines "History of Spanish slavery in the Philippines") and forced crew,[^73] whereas many [Latin Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_American_Asian "Latin American Asian") were brought to the Philippines as soldiers and colonists.[^74] The Philippines hosts the only Latin American established districts in Asia.[^75] [^76] [Spanish Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intramuros "Intramuros") became the capital of the [Captaincy General of the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_the_Philippines "Captaincy General of the Philippines") and the [Spanish East Indies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies "Spanish East Indies") in 1571,[^77] [^78] Spanish territories in Asia and the Pacific.[^79] The Spanish invaded local states using the principle of [divide and conquer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divide_and_rule "Divide and rule"),[^69]<sup><span title="Page: 374">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=wmgX9M_yETIC&amp;pg=PA374">374</a> </span></sup> bringing most of what is the present-day Philippines under one unified administration.[^80] [^81]

Disparate barangays were deliberately [consolidated into towns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reductions "Reductions"), where [Catholic missionaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friars_in_Spanish_Philippines "Friars in Spanish Philippines") could more easily convert their inhabitants to [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity "Christianity"),[^82]<sup><span title="Pages: 53, 68">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=xiOQdEzgP9kC&amp;pg=PA53">53</a>, <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=xiOQdEzgP9kC&amp;pg=PA68">68</a> </span></sup> [^83] which was initially [Syncretist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_Syncretism "Religious Syncretism").[^84] [Christianization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianization "Christianization") by the [Spanish friars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friars_in_Spanish_Philippines "Friars in Spanish Philippines") occurred mostly across the settled lowlands over the course of time. From 1565 to 1821, the Philippines was governed as a territory of the [Mexico City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico_City "Mexico City") -based Viceroyalty of New Spain; it was then administered from [Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrid "Madrid") after the [Mexican War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence "Mexican War of Independence").[^85]<sup><span title="Page: 81">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gUt5v8ET4QYC&amp;pg=PA81">81</a> </span></sup> Manila became the western hub of [trans-Pacific trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet "Spanish treasure fleet") [^86] by [Manila galleons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila_galleon "Manila galleon") built in [Bicol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicol_Region "Bicol Region") and [Cavite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cavite "Cavite").[^87] [^88]

During its rule, Spain spent a significant sum of its treasury quelling [indigenous revolts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_revolts_against_Spain "Philippine revolts against Spain") [^85]<sup><span title="Pages: 111–122">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gUt5v8ET4QYC&amp;pg=PA111">111–122</a> </span></sup> and defending against external military attacks,[^89]<sup><span title="Page: 1077">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1077">1077</a> </span></sup> [^90] including [Moro piracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Sulu_and_Celebes_Seas "Piracy in the Sulu and Celebes Seas"),[^91] a 17th-century [war against the Dutch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_La_Naval_de_Manila "Battles of La Naval de Manila"), 18th-century [British occupation of Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_occupation_of_Manila "British occupation of Manila"), and conflict with Muslims in the south.[^92]<sup><span title="Location: 4">: <a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060927161256/http://countrystudies.us/philippines/4.htm">4</a></span></sup>

Administration of the Philippines was considered a drain on the economy of New Spain,[^89]<sup><span title="Page: 1077">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1077">1077</a> </span></sup> and abandoning it or trading it for other territory was debated. This course of action was opposed because of the islands' economic potential, security, and the desire to continue religious conversion in the region.[^64]<sup><span title="Pages: 7–8">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=A40BEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA7">7–8</a> </span></sup> [^93] The colony survived on an annual subsidy from the Spanish crown [^89]<sup><span title="Page: 1077">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1077">1077</a> </span></sup> averaging 250,000 pesos,[^64]<sup><span title="Page: 8">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=A40BEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA8">8</a> </span></sup> usually paid as 75 tons of silver bullion from the Americas.[^94] [British forces occupied Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_occupation_of_Manila "British occupation of Manila") from 1762 to 1764 during the [Seven Years' War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War "Seven Years' War"). Spanish rule was restored with the [1763 Treaty of Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_\(1763\) "Treaty of Paris (1763)").[^72]<sup><span title="Pages: 81–83">: 81–83</span> </sup> The Spanish considered their war with the Muslims in Southeast Asia an extension of the *[Reconquista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconquista "Reconquista")*.[^95] [^96] The [Spanish–Moro conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93Moro_conflict "Spanish–Moro conflict") lasted for several hundred years. Spain conquered portions of [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao") and [Jolo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jolo "Jolo") during the last quarter of the 19th century,[^97] and the Muslim [Moro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_people "Moro people") in the [Sultanate of Sulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Sulu "Sultanate of Sulu") acknowledged Spanish sovereignty.[^98] [^99]

![Photo of a large group of men on steps. Some are seated, and others are standing; several are wearing top hats.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ilustrados_1890.jpg/330px-Ilustrados_1890.jpg)

Ilustrados in Madrid around 1890

Philippine ports opened to world trade during the 19th century, and Filipino society began to change.[^100] [^101] Social identity changed, with the term *Filipino* encompassing all residents of the archipelago instead of solely referring to [Spaniards born in the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Filipino "Spanish Filipino").[^102] [^103]

Revolutionary sentiment grew in 1872 after 200 locally recruited [colonial troops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_troops "Colonial troops") and laborers alongside [three activist Catholic priests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gomburza "Gomburza") were executed on [questionable grounds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1872_Cavite_mutiny "1872 Cavite mutiny").[^104] [^105] This inspired the [Propaganda Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propaganda_Movement "Propaganda Movement"), organized by [Marcelo H. del Pilar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcelo_H._del_Pilar "Marcelo H. del Pilar"), [José Rizal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal "José Rizal"), [Graciano López Jaena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graciano_L%C3%B3pez_Jaena "Graciano López Jaena"), and [Mariano Ponce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariano_Ponce "Mariano Ponce"), which advocated political reform in the Philippines.[^106] Rizal was executed on December 30, 1896, for rebellion, and his death radicalized many who had been loyal to Spain.[^107] Attempts at reform met with resistance; [Andrés Bonifacio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio "Andrés Bonifacio") founded the [Katipunan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katipunan "Katipunan") secret society, which sought independence from Spain through armed revolt, in 1892.[^85]<sup><span title="Pages: 137">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gUt5v8ET4QYC&amp;pg=PA137">137</a></span></sup>

The Katipunan [Cry of Pugad Lawin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cry_of_Pugad_Lawin "Cry of Pugad Lawin") began the [Philippine Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Revolution "Philippine Revolution") in 1896.[^108] Internal disputes led to the [Tejeros Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tejeros_Convention "Tejeros Convention"), at which Bonifacio lost his position and [Emilio Aguinaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo "Emilio Aguinaldo") was elected the new leader of the revolution.[^109]<sup><span title="Pages: 145–147">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=4wk8yqCEmJUC&amp;pg=PA147">145–147</a> </span></sup> The 1897 [Pact of Biak-na-Bato](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pact_of_Biak-na-Bato "Pact of Biak-na-Bato") resulted in the [Hong Kong Junta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_Junta "Hong Kong Junta") government in exile. The [Spanish–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War "Spanish–American War") began the following year, and reached the Philippines; Aguinaldo returned, resumed the revolution, and [declared independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Declaration_of_Independence "Philippine Declaration of Independence") from Spain on June 12, 1898.[^110]<sup><span title="Page: 26">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=0Hd3EAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA26">26</a> </span></sup> In December 1898, the islands were [ceded by Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_\(1898\) "Treaty of Paris (1898)") to the United States with [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico") and [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam") after the [Spanish–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War "Spanish–American War").[^111] [^112] [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain "Spain") had ruled the Philippines for 333 years.[^113]

The [First Philippine Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic "First Philippine Republic") was promulgated on January 21, 1899.[^114] Lack of recognition by the United States led to an [outbreak of hostilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_\(1899\) "Battle of Manila (1899)") that, after refusal by the U.S. on-scene military commander of a cease-fire proposal and a declaration of war by the nascent Republic,[^8] escalated into the [Philippine–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War "Philippine–American War").[^115] [^116] [^117] [^118]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/General_Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_troops_in_Pampanga_c1898.jpg/250px-General_Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_troops_in_Pampanga_c1898.jpg)

Filipino General Gregorio del Pilar and his troops in Pampanga around 1898, during the Philippine-American War

The war resulted in the deaths of 250,000 to 1 million civilians, primarily due to famine and disease.[^119] Many Filipinos were transported by the Americans to [concentration camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_concentration_and_internment_camps#Philippines "List of concentration and internment camps"), where thousands died.[^120] [^121] After the fall of the First Philippine Republic in 1902, an [American civilian government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insular_Government_of_the_Philippine_Islands "Insular Government of the Philippine Islands") was established with the [Philippine Organic Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Organic_Act_\(1902\) "Philippine Organic Act (1902)").[^122] American forces continued to secure and extend their control of the islands, suppressing an attempted [extension of the Philippine Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tagalog_Republic#Sakay "Tagalog Republic"),[^109]<sup><span title="Pages: 200–202">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=4wk8yqCEmJUC&amp;pg=PA200">200–202</a> </span></sup> [^119] [securing the Sultanate of Sulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiram%E2%80%93Bates_Treaty "Kiram–Bates Treaty"),[^123] [^124] establishing control of interior mountainous areas which had resisted Spanish conquest,[^125] and encouraging large-scale resettlement of Christians in once-predominantly-Muslim Mindanao.[^126] [^127]

### Commonwealth and World War II (1935–1946)

Cultural developments in the Philippines strengthened a national identity,[^128] [^129]<sup><span title="Page: 12">: 12</span> </sup> and [Tagalog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tagalog_language "Tagalog language") began to take precedence over other local languages.[^82]<sup><span title="Page: 121">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=xiOQdEzgP9kC&amp;pg=PA121">121</a> </span></sup> Governmental functions were gradually given to Filipinos by the [Taft Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taft_Commission "Taft Commission");[^89]<sup><span title="Pages: 1081, 1117">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1081">1081</a>, <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1117">1117</a> </span></sup> the 1934 [Tydings–McDuffie Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tydings%E2%80%93McDuffie_Act "Tydings–McDuffie Act") granted a ten-year transition to independence through the creation of the Commonwealth of the Philippines the following year,[^130] with [Manuel Quezon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon "Manuel L. Quezon") president and [Sergio Osmeña](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Osme%C3%B1a "Sergio Osmeña") vice president.[^131] Quezon's priorities were defence, social justice, inequality, economic diversification, and national character.[^89]<sup><span title="Pages: 1081, 1117">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1081">1081</a>, <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QKgraWbb7yoC&amp;pg=PA1117">1117</a> </span></sup> [Filipino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filipino_language "Filipino language") (a standardized variety of Tagalog) became the national language,[^132]<sup><span title="Pages: 27–29">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=W1h9oF9rj-MC&amp;pg=PA27">27–29</a> </span></sup> [women's suffrage was introduced](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1937_Philippine_women%27s_suffrage_plebiscite "1937 Philippine women's suffrage plebiscite"),[^133] [^69]<sup><span title="Page: 416">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=wmgX9M_yETIC&amp;pg=PA416">416</a> </span></sup> and [land reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_reform_in_the_Philippines "Land reform in the Philippines") was considered.[^134] [^135] [^136] The introduction of women's suffrage during the Commonwealth period (1935–1946) signifies a progressive step towards [gender equality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_equality "Gender equality") in the Philippines. This gave women the right to vote and participate in the country's political processes.

![Douglas MacArthur, Sergio Osmeña, and Osmeña's staff wading ashore in knee-deep water](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/250px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg)

General Douglas MacArthur and Sergio Osmeña (left) coming ashore during the Battle of Leyte on October 20, 1944

The [Empire of Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan") invaded the Philippines in December 1941 [during World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_history_of_the_Philippines_during_World_War_II "Military history of the Philippines during World War II"),[^137] and the [Second Philippine Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Philippine_Republic "Second Philippine Republic") was established as a [puppet state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puppet_state "Puppet state") governed by [Jose P. Laurel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jose_P._Laurel "Jose P. Laurel").[^138] [^139] Beginning in 1942, the [Japanese occupation of the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Philippines "Japanese occupation of the Philippines") was [opposed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_resistance_against_Japan "Philippine resistance against Japan") by large-scale [underground guerrilla activity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Philippines#Resistance "Japanese occupation of the Philippines").[^140] [^141] [^142] [Atrocities and war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes "Japanese war crimes") were committed during the war, including the [Bataan Death March](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bataan_Death_March "Bataan Death March") and the [Manila massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila_massacre "Manila massacre").[^143] [^144] The Philippine resistance and Allied troops [defeated the Japanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines_campaign_\(1944%E2%80%931945\) "Philippines campaign (1944–1945)") in 1944 and 1945. Over one million Filipinos were estimated to have died by the end of the war.[^145] [^146] On October 11, 1945, the Philippines became a [founding member](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations "Member states of the United Nations") of the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations").[^147] [^148]<sup><span title="Pages: 38–41">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Ty7NAG1Jl-8C&amp;pg=PA38">38–41</a> </span></sup> On July 4, 1946, during the presidency of [Manuel Roxas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Roxas "Manuel Roxas"), the country's independence was recognized by the United States with the [Treaty of Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Manila_\(1946\) "Treaty of Manila (1946)").[^148]<sup><span title="Pages: 38–41">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Ty7NAG1Jl-8C&amp;pg=PA38">38–41</a> </span></sup> [^149]

### Independence (1946–present)

Efforts at post-war reconstruction and ending the [Hukbalahap Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hukbalahap_Rebellion "Hukbalahap Rebellion") succeeded during [Ramon Magsaysay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramon_Magsaysay "Ramon Magsaysay") 's presidency,[^150] but sporadic communist insurgency continued to flare up long afterward.[^151] Under Magsaysay's successor, [Carlos P. Garcia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_P._Garcia "Carlos P. Garcia"), the government initiated a [Filipino First policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filipino_First_policy "Filipino First policy") which promoted Filipino-owned businesses.[^82]<sup><span title="Page: 182">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=xiOQdEzgP9kC&amp;pg=PA182">182</a> </span></sup> Succeeding Garcia, [Diosdado Macapagal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diosdado_Macapagal "Diosdado Macapagal") moved Independence Day from July 4 to June 12—the date of Emilio Aguinaldo's declaration— [^152] and pursued [a claim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Borneo_dispute "North Borneo dispute") on eastern [North Borneo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Borneo "North Borneo").[^153] [^154]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/CongressBuilding_SEATO.jpg/250px-CongressBuilding_SEATO.jpg)

The attending leaders of the Manila Summit Conference in front of the Congress Building in Manila, hosted by Ferdinand Marcos on October 24, 1966

In 1965, Macapagal [lost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1965_Philippine_presidential_election "1965 Philippine presidential election") the presidential election to [Ferdinand Marcos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_Marcos "Ferdinand Marcos"). [Early in his presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_term_of_the_presidency_of_Ferdinand_Marcos "First term of the presidency of Ferdinand Marcos"), Marcos began infrastructure projects funded mostly by foreign loans; this improved the economy, and contributed to his [reelection in 1969](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969_Philippine_presidential_election "1969 Philippine presidential election").[^155]<sup><span title="Page: 58">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=NkBO2RhI4NUC&amp;pg=PA58">58</a> </span></sup> [^156] Near the end of his last constitutionally-permitted term, Marcos [declared martial law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proclamation_No._1081 "Proclamation No. 1081") on September 21, 1972 [^157] using the specter of communism [^158] [^159] [^160] and began to [rule by decree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_by_decree "Rule by decree");[^161] the period was characterized by [political repression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_detainees_under_the_Marcos_dictatorship "Political detainees under the Marcos dictatorship"), [censorship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journalism_during_the_Marcos_dictatorship "Journalism during the Marcos dictatorship"), and [human rights violations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_abuses_of_the_Marcos_dictatorship "Human rights abuses of the Marcos dictatorship").[^162] [^163] [Monopolies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monopolies_in_the_Philippines_\(1965%E2%80%931986\) "Monopolies in the Philippines (1965–1986)") controlled by [Marcos's cronies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cronies_of_Ferdinand_Marcos "Cronies of Ferdinand Marcos") were established in key industries,[^164] [^165] [^166] including [logging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation_in_the_Philippines#Deforestation_during_the_martial_law_era "Deforestation in the Philippines") [^167] and broadcasting;[^69]<sup><span title="Page: 120">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=wmgX9M_yETIC&amp;pg=PA120">120</a> </span></sup> a sugar monopoly led to [a famine on the island of Negros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negros_famine "Negros famine").[^168] With his wife, [Imelda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imelda_Marcos "Imelda Marcos"), Marcos was accused of corruption and [embezzling billions of dollars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unexplained_wealth_of_the_Marcos_family "Unexplained wealth of the Marcos family") of public funds.[^169] [^170] Marcos's heavy borrowing [early in his presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969_Philippine_balance_of_payments_crisis "1969 Philippine balance of payments crisis") resulted in [economic crashes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Philippines_\(1965%E2%80%931986\) "Economic history of the Philippines (1965–1986)"), exacerbated by an [early 1980s recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_1980s_recession "Early 1980s recession") where the economy contracted by 7.3 percent annually in 1984 and 1985.[^171]<sup><span title="Page: 212">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=DmkPEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA212">212</a> </span></sup> [^172]

On August 21, 1983, opposition leader [Benigno Aquino Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino "Ninoy Aquino") (Marcos's chief rival) was [assassinated on the tarmac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Ninoy_Aquino "Assassination of Ninoy Aquino") at [Manila International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_International_Airport "Ninoy Aquino International Airport").[^173] Marcos called a snap [presidential election in 1986](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_Philippine_presidential_election "1986 Philippine presidential election") [^174] which proclaimed him the winner, but the results were widely regarded as fraudulent.[^175] The resulting protests led to the [People Power Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People_Power_Revolution "People Power Revolution"),[^176] [^177] which forced Marcos and his allies to flee to [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii "Hawaii"). Aquino's widow, [Corazon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corazon_Aquino "Corazon Aquino"), was installed as president [^176] and a new constitution was promulgated.[^178]

The return of democracy and government reforms which began in 1986 were hampered by [national debt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_debt_of_the_Philippines "National debt of the Philippines"), government corruption, and [coup attempts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coup_attempts_against_Corazon_Aquino "Coup attempts against Corazon Aquino").[^179] [^155]<sup><span title="Pages: xii, xiii">: xii, xiii</span> </sup> A [communist insurgency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_rebellion_in_the_Philippines "Communist rebellion in the Philippines") [^180] [^181] and military conflict with [Moro separatists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_conflict "Moro conflict") persisted;[^182] the administration also faced a series of disasters, including the eruption of [Mount Pinatubo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Pinatubo "Mount Pinatubo") in June 1991.[^183] Aquino was succeeded by [Fidel V. Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_V._Ramos "Fidel V. Ramos"), who [liberalized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_liberalization "Economic liberalization") the national economy with [privatization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privatization "Privatization") and [deregulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deregulation "Deregulation").[^184] [^185] Ramos's economic gains were overshadowed by the onset of the [1997 Asian financial crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis "1997 Asian financial crisis").[^186] [^187] His successor, [Joseph Estrada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Estrada "Joseph Estrada"), prioritized public housing [^188] but faced corruption allegations [^189] which led to his overthrow by the [2001 EDSA Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_EDSA_Revolution "Second EDSA Revolution") and the succession of Vice President [Gloria Macapagal Arroyo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo "Gloria Macapagal Arroyo") on January 20, 2001.[^190]

Arroyo's [nine-year administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo "Presidency of Gloria Macapagal Arroyo") was marked by economic growth,[^20] but was tainted by corruption and political scandals,[^191] [^192] including [electoral fraud allegations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_Garci_scandal "Hello Garci scandal") during the [2004 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Philippine_presidential_election "2004 Philippine presidential election").[^193] Economic growth continued during [Benigno Aquino III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III "Benigno Aquino III") 's administration, which advocated good governance and transparency.[^194]<sup><span title="Pages: 1, 3">: 1, 3</span> </sup> [^195] Aquino III signed [a peace agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comprehensive_Agreement_on_the_Bangsamoro "Comprehensive Agreement on the Bangsamoro") with the [Moro Islamic Liberation Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_Islamic_Liberation_Front "Moro Islamic Liberation Front") (MILF) resulting in the [Bangsamoro Organic Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangsamoro_Organic_Law "Bangsamoro Organic Law") establishing an autonomous [Bangsamoro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangsamoro "Bangsamoro") region, but a [shootout with MILF rebels in Mamasapano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamasapano_clash "Mamasapano clash") delayed passage of the law.[^196] [^197]

Growing public frustration with post- [EDSA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People_Power_Revolution "People Power Revolution") governance led to the [2016 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Philippine_presidential_election "2016 Philippine presidential election") [^198] of populist [Rodrigo Duterte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rodrigo_Duterte "Rodrigo Duterte"),[^199] [^200] whose [presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Rodrigo_Duterte "Presidency of Rodrigo Duterte") saw the decline of [liberalism in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_Philippines "Liberalism in the Philippines") albeit largely retaining liberal economic policies.[^201] [^202] Among Duterte's priorities was [aggressively increasing infrastructure spending](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Build!_Build!_Build! "Build! Build! Build!") to spur economic growth;[^203] [^204] the enactment of the Bangsamoro Organic Law;[^205] an intensified crackdown on crime and communist insurgencies;[^206] and [an anti-drug campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_drug_war "Philippine drug war") that reduced drug proliferation [^207] but that has also led to [extrajudicial killings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extrajudicial_killing "Extrajudicial killing").[^208] [^209] In early 2020, the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_Philippines "COVID-19 pandemic in the Philippines") reached the Philippines,[^210] [^211] necessitating [nationwide lockdowns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_community_quarantines_in_the_Philippines "COVID-19 community quarantines in the Philippines") that caused a brief but severe [economic recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_recession "COVID-19 recession").[^212] [^213] Under a promise of continuing Duterte's policies,[^202] Marcos's son, [Bongbong Marcos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bongbong_Marcos "Bongbong Marcos"), ran with Duterte's daughter, [Sara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sara_Duterte "Sara Duterte"), and won the [2022 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Philippine_presidential_election "2022 Philippine presidential election").[^214] Marcos's renewal of a pro-US foreign policy, however, has been viewed as a reversal of Duterte's cordiality with China, and [territorial disputes in the South China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_disputes_in_the_South_China_Sea "Territorial disputes in the South China Sea") have since escalated.[^215] The Marcos administration also [arrested](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrest_of_Rodrigo_Duterte "Arrest of Rodrigo Duterte") his predecessor Duterte, who was sent to the [International Criminal Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Criminal_Court "International Criminal Court") in [The Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Netherlands "The Netherlands") for trial of [crimes against humanity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity "Crimes against humanity"), which led to the collapse of the Marcos-Duterte alliance. Later on, a series of [corruption, mismanagement and irregularities in government-funded flood management projects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flood_control_projects_controversy_in_the_Philippines "Flood control projects controversy in the Philippines") occurred under his administration, resulting in [numerous protests nationwide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_2025_Philippine_protests "September 2025 Philippine protests"). The country suffered an [energy crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_energy_crisis_in_the_Philippines "2026 energy crisis in the Philippines") as a result of the [conflict in Middle East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_war "2026 Iran war").

## Geography

![Map of the Philippines, color-coded by elevation](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Relief_Map_Of_The_Philippines.png/250px-Relief_Map_Of_The_Philippines.png)

The Philippines is generally mountainous. Uplands make up 65 percent of the Philippines's land area. 61: 38 216

The Philippines is an archipelago of approximately [7,641 islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Philippines "List of islands of the Philippines"),[^217] [^218] covering a total area (including inland bodies of water) of about 300,000 square kilometers (115,831 sq mi).[^219] [^220]<sup><span title="Page: 15">: 15</span> </sup> [^20] [^5] Stretching 1,850 kilometers (1,150 mi) north to south,[^222] from the [South China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea "South China Sea") to the [Celebes Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celebes_Sea "Celebes Sea"),[^223] the Philippines [is bordered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borders_of_the_Philippines "Borders of the Philippines") by the [Philippine Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Sea "Philippine Sea") to the east,[^224] [^225] and the [Sulu Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulu_Sea "Sulu Sea") to the southwest.[^226] The [Luzon Strait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luzon_Strait "Luzon Strait") is the most economical (quickest) traffic node for shipping between the [Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas "Americas") and [Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia "Asia").[^227] [^228] [^229] It is also a critical [junction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_junction "Electrical junction") of Asia-Pacific-Americas [undersea communication cables](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undersea_communication_cable "Undersea communication cable").[^230] [^231] [^232] [^233] The [country's 11 largest islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Philippines "List of islands of the Philippines") are [Luzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luzon "Luzon"), [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao"), [Samar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samar "Samar"), [Negros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negros "Negros"), [Palawan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palawan_\(island\) "Palawan (island)"), [Panay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panay "Panay"), [Mindoro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindoro "Mindoro"), [Leyte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leyte "Leyte"), [Cebu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cebu_\(island\) "Cebu (island)"), [Bohol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohol "Bohol") and [Masbate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masbate_\(island\) "Masbate (island)"), about 95 percent of its total land area.[^234] The Philippines' coastline measures 36,289 kilometers (22,549 mi), the world's [fifth-longest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_length_of_coastline "List of countries by length of coastline"),[^235] and the [country's exclusive economic zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone_of_the_Philippines "Exclusive economic zone of the Philippines") covers 2,263,816 km <sup>2</sup> (874,064 sq mi).[^236]

Its [highest mountain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_the_Philippines "List of mountains in the Philippines") is [Mount Apo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Apo "Mount Apo") on Mindanao, with an altitude of 2,954 meters (9,692 ft) above sea level.[^20] The Philippines' [longest river](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_the_Philippines "List of rivers of the Philippines") is the [Cagayan River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cagayan_River "Cagayan River") in northern Luzon, which flows for about 520 kilometers (320 mi).[^237] [Manila Bay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila_Bay "Manila Bay"), on which is the capital city of [Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila "Manila"),[^238] is connected to [Laguna de Bay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laguna_de_Bay "Laguna de Bay") [^239] (the country's [largest lake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_lakes_of_the_Philippines "List of lakes of the Philippines")) by the [Pasig River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pasig_River "Pasig River").[^240]

On the western fringes of the Pacific [Ring of Fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ring_of_Fire "Ring of Fire"), the Philippines has frequent seismic and volcanic activity.[^241]<sup><span title="Page: 4">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=y1CVR74_KHQC&amp;pg=PA4">4</a> </span></sup> The region is [seismically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seismology "Seismology") active, and has been [constructed by plates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subduction_tectonics_of_the_Philippines "Subduction tectonics of the Philippines") converging towards each other from multiple directions.[^242] [^243] About five earthquakes are recorded daily, although most are too weak to be felt.[^244] The [last major earthquakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_the_Philippines "List of earthquakes in the Philippines") were in 1976 in the [Moro Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1976_Moro_Gulf_earthquake "1976 Moro Gulf earthquake") and in 1990 on [Luzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_Luzon_earthquake "1990 Luzon earthquake").[^245] The Philippines has [23 active volcanoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_active_volcanoes_in_the_Philippines "List of active volcanoes in the Philippines"); of them, [Mayon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayon "Mayon"), [Taal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taal_Volcano "Taal Volcano"), [Canlaon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Canlaon "Mount Canlaon"), and [Bulusan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Bulusan "Mount Bulusan") have the largest number of recorded eruptions.[^246] [^220]<sup><span title="Page: 26">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=90C4DgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA26">26</a></span></sup>

The country has valuable [^247] mineral deposits as a result of its complex geologic structure and high level of seismic activity.[^248] [^249] It is thought to have the world's second-largest gold deposits (after South Africa), large copper deposits,[^250] and the world's largest deposits of [palladium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palladium "Palladium").[^251] The country's gold production in 2015 is 21 metric tonnes.[^252] Other minerals include [chromium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromium "Chromium"), [nickel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nickel "Nickel"), [molybdenum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molybdenum "Molybdenum"), [platinum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platinum "Platinum"), and [zinc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinc "Zinc").[^253] However, poor management and law enforcement, opposition from indigenous communities, and past environmental damage have left these resources largely untapped.[^250] [^254]

### Biodiversity

![Water buffalo with large, curved horns, seen from above](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Carabao.jpg/250px-Carabao.jpg)

The carabao is the national animal of the Philippines. It symbolizes strength, power, efficiency, perseverance and hard work. 255

The Philippines is a [megadiverse country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_countries "Megadiverse countries"),[^256] [^257] with some of the world's highest rates of discovery and [endemism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_ecoregions_with_high_endemism "List of ecoregions with high endemism") (67 percent).[^258] [^259] With an [estimated 13,500 plant species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flora_of_the_Philippines "Flora of the Philippines") in the country (3,500 of which are endemic),[^260] Philippine rain forests have an array of flora:[^261] [^262] about 3,500 species of trees,[^263] 8,000 [flowering plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowering_plant "Flowering plant") species, 1,100 [ferns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fern "Fern"), and 998 [orchid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_orchids_of_the_Philippines "List of the orchids of the Philippines") species [^264] have been identified.[^265] The Philippines has 167 terrestrial [mammals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal "Mammal") (102 endemic species), 235 [reptiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reptile "Reptile") (160 endemic species), 99 [amphibians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian "Amphibian") (74 endemic species), 686 [birds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_birds_of_the_Philippines "List of birds of the Philippines") (224 endemic species),[^266] and over 20,000 [insect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insect "Insect") species.[^265]

As an important part of the [Coral Triangle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral_Triangle "Coral Triangle") ecoregion,[^267] [^268] Philippine waters have unique, diverse marine life [^269] and the world's greatest diversity of shore-fish species.[^270] The country has over 3,200 fish species, 121 endemic.[^271] Philippine waters sustain [the cultivation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aquaculture_in_the_Philippines "Aquaculture in the Philippines") of fish, crustaceans, oysters, and seaweeds.[^272] [^273]

Eight major types of forests are distributed throughout the Philippines: [dipterocarp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dipterocarpaceae "Dipterocarpaceae"), [beach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beach "Beach") forest,[^274] [pine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pine "Pine") forest, [molave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitex_parviflora "Vitex parviflora") forest, [lower montane forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montane_ecosystems "Montane ecosystems"), upper montane (or [mossy forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_forest "Cloud forest")), [mangroves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mangrove "Mangrove"), and [ultrabasic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultramafic_rock "Ultramafic rock") forest.[^275] According to official estimates, the Philippines had 7,000,000 hectares (27,000 sq mi) of forest cover in 2023.[^276] Logging had been systemized during the American colonial period [^277] and [deforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation_in_the_Philippines "Deforestation in the Philippines") continued after independence, accelerating during the [Marcos presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law_under_Ferdinand_Marcos "Martial law under Ferdinand Marcos") due to unregulated logging concessions.[^278] [^279] Forest cover declined from 70 percent of the Philippines' total land area in 1900 to about 18.3 percent in 1999.[^280] Rehabilitation efforts have had marginal success.[^281]

The Philippines is a [priority hotspot for biodiversity conservation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot "Biodiversity hotspot");[^282] [^256] it has [more than 200 protected areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_the_Philippines "List of protected areas of the Philippines"),[^283] which was expanded to 7,790,000 hectares (30,100 sq mi) as of 2023.[^284] [Three sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_the_Philippines "List of World Heritage Sites in the Philippines") in the Philippines have been included on the UNESCO World Heritage List: the [Tubbataha Reef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tubbataha_Reef "Tubbataha Reef") in the Sulu Sea,[^285] the [Puerto Princesa Subterranean River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Princesa_Subterranean_River_National_Park "Puerto Princesa Subterranean River National Park"),[^286] and the [Mount Hamiguitan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Hamiguitan "Mount Hamiguitan") Wildlife Sanctuary.[^287]

### Climate

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Thunderstorms-Philippines.jpg/250px-Thunderstorms-Philippines.jpg)

Evening thunderstorms bringing rain over the Philippines are common from June to November.

The Philippines has a tropical maritime climate which is usually hot and humid. There are three seasons: a hot [dry season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_season "Dry season") from March to May, a [rainy season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wet_season "Wet season") from June to November, and a cool dry season from December to February.[^288] The southwest [monsoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsoon "Monsoon") (known as the *habagat*) lasts from May to October. The northeast monsoon (*[amihan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amihan "Amihan")*) lasts from November to April.[^289]<sup><span title="Pages: 24–25">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=sY7EBAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA24">24–25</a></span></sup>

The coolest month is January, and the warmest is May. Temperatures at sea level across the Philippines tend to be in the same range, regardless of latitude. The average annual temperature is around 26.6 °C (79.9 °F). It is 18.3 °C (64.9 °F) in [Baguio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baguio "Baguio"), 1,500 meters (4,900 ft) above sea level.[^290] The country's average [humidity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humidity "Humidity") is 82 percent.[^289]<sup><span title="Pages: 24–25">: <a href="https://books.google.com/books?id=sY7EBAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA24">24–25</a> </span></sup> Annual rainfall is as high as 5,000 millimeters (200 in) on the mountainous east coast, but less than 1,000 millimeters (39 in) in some sheltered valleys.[^288]

The [Philippine Area of Responsibility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Area_of_Responsibility "Philippine Area of Responsibility") has 19 [typhoons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoons_in_the_Philippines "Typhoons in the Philippines") in a typical year,[^291] usually from July to October.[^288] Eight or nine of them make [landfall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landfall "Landfall").[^292] [^293] The wettest recorded typhoon to hit the Philippines dropped 2,210 millimeters (87 in) in Baguio from July 14 to 18, 1911.[^294] The country [is among](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Philippines "Climate change in the Philippines") the world's ten most [vulnerable to climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability "Climate change vulnerability").[^295] [^296]

## Government and politics

![Large white-and-red building on a river](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28local_img%29.jpg/250px-Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28local_img%29.jpg)

Malacañang Palace is the president's official residence.

[^1]: Although the Flag and Heraldic Code of the Philippines (Republic Act 8491) passed in 1998 defined modifications to the coat of arms that removed the colonial charges, a referendum legally required to ratify the changes has not yet been called.

[^2]: While [Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila "Manila") is designated as [the nation's capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_of_the_Philippines "Capital of the Philippines"), the [seat of government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seat_of_government "Seat of government") is the *National Capital Region*, commonly known as " [Metro Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metro_Manila "Metro Manila") ", of which the city of Manila is a part.[^12] [^13] Many national government institutions are located on various parts of Metro Manila, aside from [Malacañang Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace "Malacañang Palace") and other institutions/agencies that are located within the Manila capital city.

[^3]: As per the 1987 Constitution: "Spanish and Arabic shall be promoted on a voluntary and optional basis." [^15]

[^5]: The actual area of the Philippines is 343,448 km <sup>2</sup> (132,606 sq mi) according to some sources.[^221]

- [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): جمهورية الفلبين, [romanized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic "Romanization of Arabic"): *Jumhūriyyat al-Filibbīn*

[^8]: This is a summary, omitting significant detail. For more detail, see [Schurman Commission § Survey visit to the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schurman_Commission#Survey_visit_to_the_Philippines "Schurman Commission").

[^10]: In the Philippines, eating with chopsticks is occasionally used, less commonly used, less frequently used, seldom used, very rarely or rarely used, or not very common, but it's perfectly acceptable, especially in certain settings. Most Filipinos use a spoon and fork as the standard utensils for eating, while chopsticks are usually reserved for Asian cuisines like Chinese, Japanese, or Korean food, particularly in restaurants that serve those dishes. At home, chopsticks aren't used daily, though some families keep them for fun or when enjoying Asian meals. There's no stigma in using chopsticks — it's even seen as interesting or "international". Just remember to use them properly, such as avoiding sticking them upright in rice, which is considered disrespectful in many Asian cultures. However, chopsticks are generally used only when eating Chinese or other Asian cuisine that traditionally requires them.

[^393]: ["Federal Systems, Intergovernmental Relations and Federated Regions"](https://www.idea.int/sites/default/files/publications/federal-systems-intergovernmental-relations-and-federated-regions.pdf) (PDF). *idea.int*. [International IDEA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Institute_for_Democracy_and_Electoral_Assistance "International Institute for Democracy and Electoral Assistance"). November 2019. Retrieved May 26, 2026. The current system of government has been in existence since Spanish colonial rule and the logic behind it then was to facilitate the extraction of goods from the colony (the Philippines) to the colonizing country (Spain). Colonial rule has now been replaced by what is referred to as 'Imperial Manila'. While there have been attempts to address this problem, such as decentralization, most of the interventions have failed since all have been confined within the current unitary form of government.
